Hi Wassim,

Thanks for your question.

When you first sign in to Ellis you should be able to see one Private Identity that has already been created, the password should be visible under the identity of the subscriber (see the attached image password 1).

When you press the ?Create? button you should be given a new Private Identity and again the password should be visible (attached image password 2).

These passwords are only visible one time, if you refresh the page or log out and log back in they will be unavailable.

Can you please try pressing the ?Create? button and comparing what you see against my attached pictures. Please let me know if the passwords are not displayed correctly.

Thanks,

Andrew

Hi Hrishikesh,

Thank you for your continued support of Project Clearwater.

Whether having a DHCP server up and running is mandatory depends on which installation method<http://clearwater.readthedocs.io/en/stable/Installation_Instructions.html> you have chosen to deploy Project Clearwater, for example the All-in-one OVF installation does require a DHCP server whereas EC2 AMI installation does not.  Could you please provide details of how you have installed Clearwater?

Checking that the nodes can ping each other is a good check for network connectivity, there are other commands you can run as well to verify the health of your deployment:


?         sudo monit summary: will display the health of various processes

?         sudo clearwater-etcdctl cluster-health: will display a list of etcd cluster member IDs and node health status

?         sudo /usr/share/clearwater/clearwater-cluster-manager/scripts/check_cluster_state: will check the state of the etcd cluster

?         sudo clearwater-check-config ?show: will display the configuration in your shared_config and local_config files and will let you know of any errors with them

If these succeed and if you can also register subscribers against your deployment and make calls that would be a good indication that your deployment is healthy. Please let me know if any of the above commands report errors.

Thanks,

Andrew

On Fri, May 19, 2017 at 3:00 PM, Andrew Edmonds <Andrew.Edmonds at metaswitch.com<mailto:Andrew.Edmonds at metaswitch.com>> wrote:
Hi Hrishikesh,

Thank you for your question.

If you look at the manual installation instructions<http://clearwater.readthedocs.io/en/stable/Manual_Install.html?highlight=apt%20Ellis> you can see that we instruct users to install Ellis by running the following commands:

sudo DEBIAN_FRONTEND=noninteractive apt-get install ellis --yes
sudo DEBIAN_FRONTEND=noninteractive apt-get install clearwater-management --yes

you can try installing Ellis again using the above commands.

There is, however, another issue with the installation I can see that you should resolve before trying this, if we look through the output of the apt-get command we can see:

usermod: user ellis is currently used by process 1222

this suggests that an existing process is causing a conflict which stops the installation from working. You can see what process 1222 is by running the command ?ps aux | grep 1222?, depending on what the process is you may be able to safely kill it and retry the installation. If there is no longer a process 1222 you can retry the installation and see if you get a similar error message for a different process ID, then you could see what that process was.

Once you have followed these steps you can retry the installation using the above commands, if the installation still does not work could you please paste me the output you get when you run the above commands.

Thanks,

Andrew

References: <CAB5XQO1LNozoTbOqDh7JxG=g5T7W=RXKUGahbuW3NosvmmpqvA@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <BY2PR02MB4413325569AFF25D6448C36E5C80@BY2PR02MB441.namprd02.prod.outlook.com>

Hi Ravi,

Thank you for your question.

The majority of the DNS requests that are required for a registration are done by the Clearwater VMs. There is only one DNS request that the external clients in Scenario B will need to do: if you have provided your Zoiper client with a hostname for the outbound proxy (which in this case will be the Bono node) the client will have to resolve this to send the register messages to Bono. This means that you may be able to fix this issue by either:


a)      including a DNS record that resolves Bono?s hostname on the rc1.com DNS server used by the clients in Scenario B



or



b)      configuring Zoiper with an IP address for the Outbound proxy

Can you try these and see if registrations start working?

If you still cannot register subscribers the issue will likely be with Bono either not receiving the register messages or not forwarding them on to the Sprout node properly. If this is the case could you please provide logs from both Bono and Sprout so we can determine what is happening here.

Thanks,

Andrew

From richard.whitehouse at projectclearwater.org  Thu Jun  8 11:38:19 2017
From: richard.whitehouse at projectclearwater.org (Richard Whitehouse (projectclearwater.org))
Date: Thu, 8 Jun 2017 15:38:19 +0000
Subject: [Project Clearwater] Sprint Galadriel Release Note
Message-ID: <BN6PR02MB33628985900C3DF017BFE937F0C90@BN6PR02MB3362.namprd02.prod.outlook.com>

Hi all,

The release for Project Clearwater sprint "Galadriel" has been cut. The code for this release is tagged as release-124 in GitHub.

In this release we have enhanced Clearwater's security by changing the way the Clearwater S-CSCF treats requests from endpoints that authenticate using the SIP digest scheme. When such an endpoint registers, the P-CSCF will typically record the IP address and port that the endpoint used. When it makes a subsequent request (such as a call setup or re-registration) the P-CSCF spots that the request is from the same IP and port and marks the request as "integrity protected" before forwarding to the S-CSCF, with the intention that the S-CSCF will not authenticate the request. Unfortunately this type of integrity protection is not completely secure - for example if another device stole a the endpoint's IP address, it could steal service. To prevent this:

. It is now possible to configure Clearwater to authenticate initial non-REGISTER requests (such as call setup requests) from these endpoints. If the request does not contain authentication information, the request is challenged with a 407 response, prompting the endpoint to re-submit its request with a proper authentication response.

To enable this behaviour, set the ` non_register_authentication` config option to ` initial_req_from_req_digest_endpoint` (see http://clearwater.readthedocs.io/en/latest/Clearwater_Configuration_Options_Reference.html for more details). 

. The S-CSCF now authenticates all REGISTER messages from these endpoints (including challenging them if necessary). 

This change is in line with Release 13 of the TS 24.229.

We also added a new feature, which gives Clearwater the ability to support Shared iFC Sets.

Shared iFC Sets are a set of iFCs, which are represented by a single number - the Shared iFC Set ID. This ID, which is much smaller than the list of iFCs it represents, can be used in place of that list both within the HSS, and over the interface between the HSS and Clearwater. This has the benefit of reducing both the used storage space in the HSS, and reducing the bandwidth of the interface between the HSS and Clearwater

We also added the ability to support barring of IMPUs (IMS Public Identities), as per TS 24.229 and TS 29.228.

Finally, this release includes the following bug fixes:

. clearwater-diags-monitor doesn't collect cassandra or memcached diags from vellum nodes
. Cassandra monitoring, provisioning and configuration isn't as expected on the new Vellum nodes
. clearwater-etcd.init.d may report warnings when used as an etcd_proxy
. A sprout alarm has misleading help text
. There should be an alias for the script gather_diags_and_report_location
. dns_config should be dns.json
. sub_max_expires should default to something similar to reg_max_expires
. Config manager does not cope with blank entries for local and remote_site_names
. Sprout will perform an ENUM lookup for the following: "wildcard-psi12321421"
. check_cluster_state reports state "in site site1" on single-site deployments

To upgrade to this release, follow the instructions at http://docs.projectclearwater.org/en/stable/Upgrading_a_Clearwater_deployment.html. ?If you are deploying an all-in-one node, the standard image (http://vm-images.cw-ngv.com/cw-aio.ova) has been updated for this release.

Richard

On Thu, Jun 1, 2017 at 6:12 PM, Andrew Edmonds <
Andrew.Edmonds at metaswitch.com> wrote:

> Hi Hrishikesh,
>
>
>
> Thank you for your continued support of Project Clearwater.
>
>
>
> Whether having a DHCP server up and running is mandatory depends on which installation
> method
> <http://clearwater.readthedocs.io/en/stable/Installation_Instructions.html>
> you have chosen to deploy Project Clearwater, for example the All-in-one
> OVF installation does require a DHCP server whereas EC2 AMI installation
> does not.  Could you please provide details of how you have installed
> Clearwater?
>
>
>
> Checking that the nodes can ping each other is a good check for network
> connectivity, there are other commands you can run as well to verify the
> health of your deployment:
>
>
>
> ?         sudo monit summary: will display the health of various processes
>
> ?         sudo clearwater-etcdctl cluster-health: will display a list of
> etcd cluster member IDs and node health status
>
> ?         sudo /usr/share/clearwater/clearwater-cluster-manager/scripts/check_cluster_state:
> will check the state of the etcd cluster
>
> ?         sudo clearwater-check-config ?show: will display the
> configuration in your shared_config and local_config files and will let you
> know of any errors with them
>
>
>
> If these succeed and if you can also register subscribers against your
> deployment and make calls that would be a good indication that your
> deployment is healthy. Please let me know if any of the above commands
> report errors.
>
>
>
> Thanks,
>
>
>
> Andrew
>
>

>
>
> Thank you for your question.
>
>
>
> If you look at the manual installation instructions
> <http://clearwater.readthedocs.io/en/stable/Manual_Install.html?highlight=apt%20Ellis>
> you can see that we instruct users to install Ellis by running the
> following commands:
>
>
>
> sudo DEBIAN_FRONTEND*=*noninteractive apt-get install ellis --yes
>
> sudo DEBIAN_FRONTEND=noninteractive apt-get install clearwater-management
> --yes
>
>
>
> you can try installing Ellis again using the above commands.
>
>
>
> There is, however, another issue with the installation I can see that you
> should resolve before trying this, if we look through the output of the
> apt-get command we can see:
>
>
>
> usermod: user ellis is currently used by process 1222
>
>
>
> this suggests that an existing process is causing a conflict which stops
> the installation from working. You can see what process 1222 is by running
> the command ?ps aux | grep 1222?, depending on what the process is you may
> be able to safely kill it and retry the installation. If there is no longer
> a process 1222 you can retry the installation and see if you get a similar
> error message for a different process ID, then you could see what that
> process was.
>
>
>
> Once you have followed these steps you can retry the installation using
> the above commands, if the installation still does not work could you
> please paste me the output you get when you run the above commands.
>
>
>
> Thanks,
>
>
>
> Andrew
>
>

From Andrew.Edmonds at metaswitch.com  Wed Jun 14 07:45:42 2017
From: Andrew.Edmonds at metaswitch.com (Andrew Edmonds)

In-Reply-To: <CAPS8sUgd22hk5KMxYOdkAwj9_UyZ1s2zrYWOtPnvoJCrf3vf_A@mail.gmail.com>
References: <CAPS8sUgd22hk5KMxYOdkAwj9_UyZ1s2zrYWOtPnvoJCrf3vf_A@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <BLUPR02MB437899F5BF0A09D6CA864C1E5C30@BLUPR02MB437.namprd02.prod.outlook.com>

Hi Alioune,

Thank you for your question and for the detailed logs you have provided.

When HTTP requests are sent to Ellis in order to provision subscribers they pass through nginx. nginx is a generic HTTP web server that should forward these HTTP requests on to Ellis. However if we look at the error logs we can see:


  - Account creation failed with HTTP code 502, body <html>

<head><title>502 Bad Gateway</title></head>

<body bgcolor="white">

<center><h1>502 Bad Gateway</h1></center>

<hr><center>nginx/1.4.6 (Ubuntu)</center>

</body>

</html>

This shows that the error is coming from nginx and it means that nginx can?t communicate with Ellis. This could be caused by one of the following:


?         The Ellis process is not running

?         Some state has got stuck that means that nginx and Ellis can?t communicate

To investigate this access your Ellis VM?s console and run ?sudo monit summary?, this will show you what processes are running . To restart nginx and the Ellis process run the commands ?sudo service nginx restart? and ?sudo service ellis restart?. If this still does not work you can check the most recent log in  /var/log/ellis and the /var/log/nginx/error.log.

Thanks,

Andrew

Hi Eric,

Thank you for your question.

Since we have updated our node types the bulk-provisioning  commands<https://github.com/Metaswitch/crest/blob/dev/docs/Bulk-Provisioning%20Numbers.md> should be run on the vellum nodes. Can you check that you get a successful output when you run the stress_provision.sh script.

You should also have your deployment configured to use homestead-prov. This will mean that subscriber details are looked up in the Cassandra database (which is where the stress_provision.sh provisions subscribers to) rather than an external HSS. To verify this can you check your /etc/clearwater/shared_config file contains the following config options:

# HSS configuration
hss_hostname=0.0.0.0
hss_port=3868

There doesn?t appear to be any errors in the Bono log you have sent me. If you try the above and still get failures could you please send me the most recent /var/log/sprout/sprout_XX log from the Sprout node?

Thanks,

Andrew

Subject: [Project Clearwater] Sipp stress test problem - 400 Bad Request

Message-ID: <CAPXxZyT13V6MSzALon=72Tq46vP0SAd1=VZkJ_pWUHSFPKk64g@mail.gmail.com>

Hi Andrew,

I've got the same problem with the lastest stable release (124). The
initial registrations are successful, so I don't think it is a problem with
the number provisioning. Moreover, excluding the re-registration part from
the scenario, the call-setup/teardown are also working. The only problem is
with the re-registration. The server replies with a 401 Unauthorized on
subsequent REGISTER messages instead of 200 OK.

No problems with the release 123.

It is possible that this problem with the sip_stress.xml scenario is due to
these changes ?


   - It is now possible to configure Clearwater to authenticate initial
   non-REGISTER requests (such as call setup requests) from these endpoints.
   If the request does not contain authentication information, the request is
   challenged with a 407 response, prompting the endpoint to re-submit its
   request with a proper authentication response.To enable this behaviour, set
   the ` non_register_authentication` config option to `
   initial_req_from_req_digest_endpoint` (see http://clearwater.readthe
   docs.io/en/latest/Clearwater_Configuration_Options_Reference.html
   <http://clearwater.readthedocs.io/en/latest/Clearwater_Configuration_Options_Reference.html>
for
   more details).


   - The S-CSCF now authenticates all REGISTER messages from these
   endpoints (including challenging them if necessary).


Thanks

Stefano

> Since we have updated our node types the bulk-provisioning  commands
> <https://github.com/Metaswitch/crest/blob/dev/docs/Bulk-Provisioning%20Numbers.md>
> should be run on the vellum nodes. Can you check that you get a successful
> output when you run the stress_provision.sh script.
>
>
>
> You should also have your deployment configured to use homestead-prov.
> This will mean that subscriber details are looked up in the Cassandra
> database (which is where the stress_provision.sh provisions subscribers to)
> rather than an external HSS. To verify this can you check your
> /etc/clearwater/shared_config file contains the following config options:
>
>
>
> *# HSS configuration*
>
> *hss*_hostname*=*0.0*.*0.0
>
> *hss*_port*=*3868
>
>
>
> There doesn?t appear to be any errors in the Bono log you have sent me. If
> you try the above and still get failures could you please send me the most
> recent /var/log/sprout/sprout_XX log from the Sprout node?
>
>
>
> Thanks,
>
>
>
> Andrew

Hi,

I finally resolve these problem.

Thank you guys.

I use vellum node to create account through bulk_autocomplete.py
and bulk_autocomplete.py in
    usr/share/clearwater/crest-prov/src/metaswitch/crest/tools/

It also can be done with command as following :
/
usr/share/clearwater/crest-prov/src/metaswitch/crest/tools/stress_provision.sh
200000

The main prolem is sip_stress.xml which is too old to processing, and
errors occur when processing re-registartion, just as Stefano said.

Thus, I delete the re-registration part in sip_stress.xml, and stress test
works well.

Thanks a lot.


Best regards,

Eric

 Shared Configuration error
In-Reply-To: <CAFwW5BHDw4bm8QBSQOSGGfOKb6QhF+2dQ5tPaZR8G9SmviaZtg@mail.gmail.com>
References: <CAFwW5BHDw4bm8QBSQOSGGfOKb6QhF+2dQ5tPaZR8G9SmviaZtg@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <BLUPR02MB43790899E9B6F67D6EDFBE6E5C10@BLUPR02MB437.namprd02.prod.outlook.com>

Hi Bader,

Thank you for your question.

Clearwater-etcd is the component responsible for forming a cluster across your Clearwater nodes to allow configuration to be shared. If there is a problem with uploading shared config, clearwater-etcd is usually a good place to start diagnosing the issue.

A good first step is to check that the clearwater-etcd process is running, if you enter the command ?sudo monit summary? you should see etcd_process reported as having status Running.

If the etcd_process it is not running you can try using the command ?sudo service clearwater-etcd start?. If this does not work could you please send me the /var/log/clearwater-etcd/clearwater-etcd.log log file.

If the etcd_process is running you can you can use some of the commands here<http://clearwater.readthedocs.io/en/stable/Troubleshooting_and_Recovery.html?#deployment-management> to inspect the state of the underlying etcd cluster used by the management system. In particular ?clearwater-etcdctl cluster-health? and ?clearwater-etcdctl member list? might be useful.

If none of the above suggestions help you upload shared config could you please also send me the contents of your shared config and local config files.

Thanks,

Andrew

From Sebastian.Rex at metaswitch.com  Mon Jun 19 07:00:04 2017
From: Sebastian.Rex at metaswitch.com (Sebastian Rex)
Date: Mon, 19 Jun 2017 11:00:04 +0000
Subject: [Project Clearwater] Release note for sprint Helm Hammerhand
Message-ID: <SN1PR02MB1664A0D9389132B489EAF8118FC40@SN1PR02MB1664.namprd02.prod.outlook.com>

The release for Project Clearwater sprint "Helm Hammerhand" has been cut. The code for this release is tagged as release-125 in GitHub.

This release includes a change to the way the PROJECT-CLEARWATER-MIB is generated. It is now built from MIB fragments in the clearwater-snmp-handlers repository. The MIB is now included in the clearwater-snmp-alarm-agent package, copied to "/usr/share/clearwater/mibs/" on installation of the package. The MIB is no longer checked in to the repository, but can be built on demand outside of the alarm agent package if required; see the clearwater-snmp-handlers readme<https://github.com/Metaswitch/clearwater-snmp-handlers/blob/master/README.md> for instructions.

This release also includes the following bug fixes:


*         Typo in S-CSCF URI defaulting code

*         Sprout crashes in URI classifier

To upgrade to this release, follow the instructions at http://docs.projectclearwater.org/en/stable/Upgrading_a_Clearwater_deployment.html.  If you are deploying an all-in-one node, the standard image (http://vm-images.cw-ngv.com/cw-aio.ova) has been updated for this release.

Seb.

2017-06-16 15:01 GMT+02:00 Andrew Edmonds <Andrew.Edmonds at metaswitch.com<mailto:Andrew.Edmonds at metaswitch.com>>:
Hi Bader,

Thank you for your question.

Clearwater-etcd is the component responsible for forming a cluster across your Clearwater nodes to allow configuration to be shared. If there is a problem with uploading shared config, clearwater-etcd is usually a good place to start diagnosing the issue.

A good first step is to check that the clearwater-etcd process is running, if you enter the command ?sudo monit summary? you should see etcd_process reported as having status Running.

If the etcd_process it is not running you can try using the command ?sudo service clearwater-etcd start?. If this does not work could you please send me the /var/log/clearwater-etcd/clearwater-etcd.log log file.

If the etcd_process is running you can you can use some of the commands here<http://clearwater.readthedocs.io/en/stable/Troubleshooting_and_Recovery.html?#deployment-management> to inspect the state of the underlying etcd cluster used by the management system. In particular ?clearwater-etcdctl cluster-health? and ?clearwater-etcdctl member list? might be useful.

If none of the above suggestions help you upload shared config could you please also send me the contents of your shared config and local config files.

Thanks,

Andrew

2017-06-14 13:45 GMT+02:00 Andrew Edmonds <Andrew.Edmonds at metaswitch.com<mailto:Andrew.Edmonds at metaswitch.com>>:
Hi Alioune,

Thank you for your question and for the detailed logs you have provided.

When HTTP requests are sent to Ellis in order to provision subscribers they pass through nginx. nginx is a generic HTTP web server that should forward these HTTP requests on to Ellis. However if we look at the error logs we can see:


  - Account creation failed with HTTP code 502, body <html>

<head><title>502 Bad Gateway</title></head>

<body bgcolor="white">

<center><h1>502 Bad Gateway</h1></center>

<hr><center>nginx/1.4.6 (Ubuntu)</center>

</body>

</html>

This shows that the error is coming from nginx and it means that nginx can?t communicate with Ellis. This could be caused by one of the following:


?         The Ellis process is not running

?         Some state has got stuck that means that nginx and Ellis can?t communicate

To investigate this access your Ellis VM?s console and run ?sudo monit summary?, this will show you what processes are running . To restart nginx and the Ellis process run the commands ?sudo service nginx restart? and ?sudo service ellis restart?. If this still does not work you can check the most recent log in  /var/log/ellis and the /var/log/nginx/error.log.

Thanks,

Andrew

Hi Alioune,

When I asked for the local_config and shared_config contained on your Bono node I was asking for the contents of the files /etc/clearwater/local_config and /etc/clearwater/shared_config. The hostnames contained in these files will be resolved via DNS lookups and will be used for communicating information between processes that may be on different nodes. This is what led me to suspect that ?icscf.? may appear in one of your config files based on the Bono logs you sent me.

You?ve included the contents of the /usr/share/clearwater/infrastructure/migration-utils/migrate_local_config and /usr/share/clearwater/infrastructure/migration-utils/migrate_shared_config in your latest email. These are scripts which can be used to sort the contents of the old style of config file we used: /etc/clearwater/config into the local_config and shared_config files. These scripts themselves do not contain any of your config.

Could you please send me the contents of /etc/clearwater/local_config and /etc/clearwater/shared_config.

Could you please also in future respond to these emails by replying to the clearwater at lists.projectclearwater.org<mailto:clearwater at lists.projectclearwater.org> address. This way our messages are saved to the mailing list archive so that if future Project Clearwater users hit a similar problem they will have a record of our conversation which could help them resolve their issue.

Thanks,

Andrew

2017-06-14 13:45 GMT+02:00 Andrew Edmonds <Andrew.Edmonds at metaswitch.com<mailto:Andrew.Edmonds at metaswitch.com>>:
Hi Alioune,

Thank you for your question and for the detailed logs you have provided.

When HTTP requests are sent to Ellis in order to provision subscribers they pass through nginx. nginx is a generic HTTP web server that should forward these HTTP requests on to Ellis. However if we look at the error logs we can see:


  - Account creation failed with HTTP code 502, body <html>

<head><title>502 Bad Gateway</title></head>

<body bgcolor="white">

<center><h1>502 Bad Gateway</h1></center>

<hr><center>nginx/1.4.6 (Ubuntu)</center>

</body>

</html>

This shows that the error is coming from nginx and it means that nginx can?t communicate with Ellis. This could be caused by one of the following:


?         The Ellis process is not running

?         Some state has got stuck that means that nginx and Ellis can?t communicate

To investigate this access your Ellis VM?s console and run ?sudo monit summary?, this will show you what processes are running . To restart nginx and the Ellis process run the commands ?sudo service nginx restart? and ?sudo service ellis restart?. If this still does not work you can check the most recent log in  /var/log/ellis and the /var/log/nginx/error.log.

Thanks,

Andrew
